Configuration → 
user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 703;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 102;
    disable_symlinks off;
    autoindex off;
    send_timeout 0;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1916;
    client_max_body_size 1287168;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options SAMEORIGIN;
            add_header X-Powered-By nginx/1.17.8;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server nginx/1.16.0;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block";
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'none'; frame-ancestors 'none';";
        }
    }
}

The underlying cause is application functionality using predictable URL/form actions in a repeatable way. The nature of the attack is that CSRF exploits the trust that a web site has for a user. By contrast, cross-site scripting (XSS) exploits the trust that a user has for a web site. Like XSS, CSRF attacks are not necessarily cross-site, but they can be. Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy. * Manually resetting nginx to stopped state

Configuration → 
user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 703;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 74;
    disable_symlinks on;
    autoindex on;
    send_timeout 1;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1296;
    client_max_body_size 2065408;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options DENY;
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/7.2.1;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server apache;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block";
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'none'; frame-ancestors 'none';";
        }
    }
}

A cross-site request forgery is an attack that involves forcing a victim to send an HTTP request to a target destination without their knowledge or intent in order to perform an action as the victim. The underlying cause is application functionality using predictable URL/form actions in a repeatable way. The nature of the attack is that CSRF exploits the trust that a web site has for a user. By contrast, cross-site scripting (XSS) exploits the trust that a user has for a web site. Like XSS, CSRF attacks are not necessarily cross-site, but they can be. Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy. 
	 Low

Configuration → 
user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1134;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 103;
    disable_symlinks off;
    autoindex off;
    send_timeout 1;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1324;
    client_max_body_size 1664000;
    server_tokens off;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options SAMEORIGIN;
            add_header X-Powered-By nginx/1.17.8;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server apache;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block";
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'none'; frame-ancestors 'none';";
        }
    }
}

worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 703;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 102;
    disable_symlinks off;
    autoindex on;
    send_timeout 1;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1916;
    client_max_body_size 1287168;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options DENY;
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/7.2.1;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server nginx/1.16.0;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block";
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'none'; frame-ancestors 'none';";
        }
    }

	 No Anti-CSRF tokens were found in a HTML submission form.
A cross-site request forgery is an attack that involves forcing a victim to send an HTTP request to a target destination without their knowledge or intent in order to perform an action as the victim. The underlying cause is application functionality using predictable URL/form actions in a repeatable way. The nature of the attack is that CSRF exploits the trust that a web site has for a user. By contrast, cross-site scripting (XSS) exploits the trust that a user has for a web site. Like XSS, CSRF attacks are not necessarily cross-site, but they can be. Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy. 
	 Low

Configuration → 
user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1166;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 30;
    disable_symlinks on;
    autoindex off;
    send_timeout 1;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1946;
    client_max_body_size 806912;
    server_tokens off;
    gzip on;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options "ALLOW-FROM http://www.exampletfm.com/";
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/7.2.1;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server caddy;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block";
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'self'; frame-ancestors 'self';";
        }
    }
}

user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;

    worker_connections 1030;
}

    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;

    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 30;
    disable_symlinks on;
    autoindex off;
    send_timeout 1;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1916;
    client_max_body_size 1286144;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;

            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }

            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options DENY;
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/5.6.8;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server apache;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection 1;
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'none'; frame-ancestors 'none';";
        }
    }
}

A cross-site request forgery is an attack that involves forcing a victim to send an HTTP request to a target destination without their knowledge or intent in order to perform an action as the victim. The underlying cause is application functionality using predictable URL/form actions in a repeatable way. The nature of the attack is that CSRF exploits the trust that a web site has for a user. By contrast, cross-site scripting (XSS) exploits the trust that a user has for a web site. Like XSS, CSRF attacks are not necessarily cross-site, but they can be. Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy. 
	 Low

Configuration → 
user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1030;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 30;
    disable_symlinks on;
    autoindex off;
    send_timeout 1;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1946;
    client_max_body_size 806912;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip on;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options DENY;
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/5.6.8;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server caddy;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection 1;
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'none'; frame-ancestors 'none';";
        }
    }
}

A cross-site request forgery is an attack that involves forcing a victim to send an HTTP request to a target destination without their knowledge or intent in order to perform an action as the victim. The underlying cause is application functionality using predictable URL/form actions in a repeatable way. The nature of the attack is that CSRF exploits the trust that a web site has for a user. By contrast, cross-site scripting (XSS) exploits the trust that a user has for a web site. Like XSS, CSRF attacks are not necessarily cross-site, but they can be. Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy. 
	 Low

Configuration → 
user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 703;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 102;
    disable_symlinks off;
    autoindex off;
    send_timeout 1;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1916;
    client_max_body_size 1287168;
    server_tokens off;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options "ALLOW-FROM http://www.exampletfm.com/";
            add_header X-Powered-By nginx/1.17.8;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server nginx/1.16.0;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block";
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'none'; frame-ancestors 'none';";
        }
    }
}

user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1134;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 10;
    disable_symlinks off;
    autoindex off;
    send_timeout 0;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1324;
    client_max_body_size 1287168;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options SAMEORIGIN;
            add_header X-Powered-By nginx/1.17.8;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server apache;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block";
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'none'; frame-ancestors 'none';";
        }
    }
}

The underlying cause is application functionality using predictable URL/form actions in a repeatable way. The nature of the attack is that CSRF exploits the trust that a web site has for a user. By contrast, cross-site scripting (XSS) exploits the trust that a user has for a web site. Like XSS, CSRF attacks are not necessarily cross-site, but they can be. Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy. * Manually resetting nginx to stopped state

Configuration → 
user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1029;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 30;
    disable_symlinks on;
    autoindex off;
    send_timeout 1;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1916;
    client_max_body_size 2065408;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options DENY;
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/5.6.8;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server caddy;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection 1;
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'none'; frame-ancestors 'none';";
        }
    }
}

user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1166;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 30;
    disable_symlinks on;
    autoindex off;
    send_timeout 1;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1946;
    client_max_body_size 806912;
    server_tokens off;
    gzip on;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options DENY;
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/7.2.1;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server caddy;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block";
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'https://*.google.com';";
        }
    }
}

A cross-site request forgery is an attack that involves forcing a victim to send an HTTP request to a target destination without their knowledge or intent in order to perform an action as the victim. The underlying cause is application functionality using predictable URL/form actions in a repeatable way. The nature of the attack is that CSRF exploits the trust that a web site has for a user. By contrast, cross-site scripting (XSS) exploits the trust that a user has for a web site. Like XSS, CSRF attacks are not necessarily cross-site, but they can be. Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy. 
	 Low

user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1030;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 30;
    disable_symlinks on;
    autoindex off;
    send_timeout 1;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1946;
    client_max_body_size 805888;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip on;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options "ALLOW-FROM http://www.exampletfm.com/";
            add_header X-Powered-By Django2.2;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options "";
            add_header Server apache;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection 1;
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'none'; frame-ancestors 'none';";
        }
    }

A cross-site request forgery is an attack that involves forcing a victim to send an HTTP request to a target destination without their knowledge or intent in order to perform an action as the victim. The underlying cause is application functionality using predictable URL/form actions in a repeatable way. The nature of the attack is that CSRF exploits the trust that a web site has for a user. By contrast, cross-site scripting (XSS) exploits the trust that a user has for a web site. Like XSS, CSRF attacks are not necessarily cross-site, but they can be. Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy. 
	 Low

user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1029;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 30;
    disable_symlinks on;
    autoindex off;
    send_timeout 1;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1916;
    client_max_body_size 1287168;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options DENY;
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/5.6.8;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server caddy;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection 1;
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'none'; frame-ancestors 'none';";
        }
    }
}

pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1134;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 10;
    disable_symlinks off;
    autoindex off;
    send_timeout 0;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1325;
    client_max_body_size 1664000;
    server_tokens off;
    gzip off;

            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options SAMEORIGIN;
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/5.6.8;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server apache;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block";

        }
    }

user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1029;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 30;
    disable_symlinks on;
    autoindex off;
    send_timeout 1;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1946;
    client_max_body_size 806912;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip on;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options "ALLOW-FROM http://www.exampletfm.com/";
            add_header X-Powered-By Django2.2;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server apache;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection 1;
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'self'; frame-ancestors 'self';";
        }
    }

A cross-site request forgery is an attack that involves forcing a victim to send an HTTP request to a target destination without their knowledge or intent in order to perform an action as the victim. The underlying cause is application functionality using predictable URL/form actions in a repeatable way. The nature of the attack is that CSRF exploits the trust that a web site has for a user. By contrast, cross-site scripting (XSS) exploits the trust that a user has for a web site. Like XSS, CSRF attacks are not necessarily cross-site, but they can be. Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy. 
	 Low

user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 705;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 102;
    disable_symlinks off;
    autoindex off;
    send_timeout 1;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1916;
    client_max_body_size 1287168;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options DENY;
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/7.2.1;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server nginx/1.16.0;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block";
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'none'; frame-ancestors 'none';";
        }
    }
}

A cross-site request forgery is an attack that involves forcing a victim to send an HTTP request to a target destination without their knowledge or intent in order to perform an action as the victim. The underlying cause is application functionality using predictable URL/form actions in a repeatable way. The nature of the attack is that CSRF exploits the trust that a web site has for a user. By contrast, cross-site scripting (XSS) exploits the trust that a user has for a web site. Like XSS, CSRF attacks are not necessarily cross-site, but they can be. Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy. * Manually resetting nginx to stopped state

user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1030;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 30;
    disable_symlinks on;
    autoindex off;
    send_timeout 1;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1916;
    client_max_body_size 806912;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip on;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options "ALLOW-FROM http://www.exampletfm.com/";
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/5.6.8;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options "";
            add_header Server caddy;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection 1;
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'none'; frame-ancestors 'none';";
        }
    }
}

Configuration → 
user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 704;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 31;
    disable_symlinks on;
    autoindex off;
    send_timeout 1;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 653;
    client_max_body_size 720896;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options DENY;
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/7.2.1;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server nginx/1.16.0;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block";
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'none'; frame-ancestors 'none';";
        }
    }
}

A cross-site request forgery is an attack that involves forcing a victim to send an HTTP request to a target destination without their knowledge or intent in order to perform an action as the victim. The underlying cause is application functionality using predictable URL/form actions in a repeatable way. The nature of the attack is that CSRF exploits the trust that a web site has for a user. By contrast, cross-site scripting (XSS) exploits the trust that a user has for a web site. Like XSS, CSRF attacks are not necessarily cross-site, but they can be. Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy. 
	 Low

Configuration → 
user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1030;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 30;
    disable_symlinks on;
    autoindex off;
    send_timeout 1;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1946;
    client_max_body_size 1664000;
    server_tokens off;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options SAMEORIGIN;
            add_header X-Powered-By Django2.2;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server apache;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block";
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'none'; frame-ancestors 'none';";
        }
    }
}

    disable_symlinks on;
    autoindex off;
    send_timeout 0;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1916;
    client_max_body_size 1287168;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;

        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;

            deny all;
        }

            deny all;
        }

            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options DENY;
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/7.2.1;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;

pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1030;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 30;
    disable_symlinks on;
    autoindex off;
    send_timeout 1;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1916;
    client_max_body_size 1287168;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;

        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;

            deny all;

            deny all;

        }

}

A cross-site request forgery is an attack that involves forcing a victim to send an HTTP request to a target destination without their knowledge or intent in order to perform an action as the victim. The underlying cause is application functionality using predictable URL/form actions in a repeatable way. The nature of the attack is that CSRF exploits the trust that a web site has for a user. By contrast, cross-site scripting (XSS) exploits the trust that a user has for a web site. Like XSS, CSRF attacks are not necessarily cross-site, but they can be. Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy. 
	 Low

A cross-site request forgery is an attack that involves forcing a victim to send an HTTP request to a target destination without their knowledge or intent in order to perform an action as the victim. The underlying cause is application functionality using predictable URL/form actions in a repeatable way. The nature of the attack is that CSRF exploits the trust that a web site has for a user. By contrast, cross-site scripting (XSS) exploits the trust that a user has for a web site. Like XSS, CSRF attacks are not necessarily cross-site, but they can be. Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy. 
	 Low

A cross-site request forgery is an attack that involves forcing a victim to send an HTTP request to a target destination without their knowledge or intent in order to perform an action as the victim. The underlying cause is application functionality using predictable URL/form actions in a repeatable way. The nature of the attack is that CSRF exploits the trust that a web site has for a user. By contrast, cross-site scripting (XSS) exploits the trust that a user has for a web site. Like XSS, CSRF attacks are not necessarily cross-site, but they can be. Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy. * Manually resetting nginx to stopped state

Configuration → 
user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 704;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 102;
    disable_symlinks off;
    autoindex off;
    send_timeout 1;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 653;
    client_max_body_size 720896;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip on;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options DENY;
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/5.6.8;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server nginx/1.16.0;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block";
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'none'; frame-ancestors 'none';";
        }
    }
}

user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1030;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 30;
    disable_symlinks on;
    autoindex off;
    send_timeout 1;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1947;
    client_max_body_size 805888;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options DENY;
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/5.3.3;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server apache;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection 1;
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'none'; frame-ancestors 'none';";
        }
    }

A cross-site request forgery is an attack that involves forcing a victim to send an HTTP request to a target destination without their knowledge or intent in order to perform an action as the victim. The underlying cause is application functionality using predictable URL/form actions in a repeatable way. The nature of the attack is that CSRF exploits the trust that a web site has for a user. By contrast, cross-site scripting (XSS) exploits the trust that a user has for a web site. Like XSS, CSRF attacks are not necessarily cross-site, but they can be. Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy. 
	 Low

user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1030;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 30;
    disable_symlinks on;
    autoindex off;
    send_timeout 1;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 653;
    client_max_body_size 720896;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options DENY;
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/7.2.1;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server apache;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection 1;
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'self'; frame-ancestors 'self';";
        }
    }
}

user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1134;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 10;
    disable_symlinks off;
    autoindex off;
    send_timeout 1;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1296;
    client_max_body_size 2064384;
    server_tokens off;
    gzip on;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options DENY;
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/5.3.3;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server apache;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block";
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'none'; frame-ancestors 'none';";
        }
    }
}

            add_header X-Frame-Options DENY;
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/5.3.3;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server apache;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block";
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'none'; frame-ancestors 'none';";
        }
    }

Alert →
	 http://www.exampletfm.com/test/upload.html 
	 <form action="../form" method="post" enctype="multipart/form-data"> 
	 No Anti-CSRF tokens were found in a HTML submission form.
A cross-site request forgery is an attack that involves forcing a victim to send an HTTP request to a target destination without their knowledge or intent in order to perform an action as the victim. The underlying cause is application functionality using predictable URL/form actions in a repeatable way. The nature of the attack is that CSRF exploits the trust that a web site has for a user. By contrast, cross-site scripting (XSS) exploits the trust that a user has for a web site. Like XSS, CSRF attacks are not necessarily cross-site, but they can be. Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy. * Manually resetting nginx to stopped state
